# Handoff to GPT — Multi-Ion Convergence Recovery (Phase 4 wall)

## Goal

Recommend the best next path forward for the fast-realignment effort.
We have a working multi-ion analytic-counterion infrastructure
(Cs⁺ + SO₄²⁻ shared-theta Bikerman closure) and a parallel-2e/4e
reaction set, but Newton diverges when we try to solve the coupled
PNP-BV system with this stack at any V_RHE in the page-15 grid
(±0.55, 0, ...). The plan lists three candidate escalation paths;
I want adversarial review on all of them and identification of any
better path I'm missing.

## Section 1 — Context bundle

### What this project is

`PNPInverse/` is a Firedrake-backed Poisson-Nernst-Planck + Butler-Volmer
forward solver for ORR (O₂ → H₂O₂ → H₂O) at pH 4 on RRDE / RDE
geometries. The production stack (May 2026) is:

  3 dynamic species (O₂, H₂O₂, H⁺)  +
  analytic counterion via Boltzmann residual on Poisson  +
  log-c primary variable (`u_i = ln c_i`)  +
  proton electrochemical-potential transformation
      (`mu_H = u_H + em·z_H·phi`)  +
  log-rate Butler-Volmer  +
  finite Stern compact layer (Robin BC)  +
  C+D orchestrator (per-V cold + z-ramp + warm-fallback).

This stack converges 15/15 over V_RHE ∈ [-0.5, +1.0] V on the LEGACY
single-counterion ClO₄⁻ + sequential R₁(O₂→H₂O₂) + R₂(H₂O₂→H₂O)
configuration.

### What we just changed (the fast-realignment plan)

Per Ruggiero 2022 J. Catal. (the deck's source paper), the experiment
is actually:
  - Cs₂SO₄ at I=0.3 M (NOT ClO₄⁻; verified by Seitz/Mangan data folder
    audit), so Cs⁺ at 199.9 mol/m³ + SO₄²⁻ at 100 mol/m³ + H⁺ at 0.1
    mol/m³ (pH 4).
  - PARALLEL ORR topology: R_2e (E°=0.695 V) + R_4e (E°=1.23 V),
    NOT sequential R₁+R₂.

Phases 0-3 of the plan landed:
  - Phase 1: disabled-reaction guard, Picard audit (works), helpers.
  - Phase 2.1: multi-counterion shared-theta closed-form in
    `Forward/bv_solver/boltzmann.py`. Replaces the old
    `len(bikerman) > 1` NotImplementedError.
  - Phase 2.2: Cs⁺/SO₄²⁻ entries in `scripts/_bv_common.py`:
        A_CSPLUS_HAT = 3.23e-5  (Cs⁺ at r=2.2 Å)
        A_SO4_HAT    = 4.20e-5  (SO₄²⁻ at r=2.4 Å)
        C_CSPLUS_HAT = 199.9 / C_SCALE  (= 166.58 with C_SCALE=1.2)
        C_SO4_HAT    = 100.0 / C_SCALE  (= 83.33)
    Verified: θ_b = 1 - A_dyn_bulk - Σ a_k c_b_k ≈ 0.991 (positive).
  - Phase 2.3: new `Forward/bv_solver/multi_ion.py` module with:
        build_counterion_ctx()  — single producer of theta_b
        solve_outer_phi_multiion()  — bisection on ρ_total(phi)=0
        compute_surface_gamma_multiion()  — multi-ion γ_s
        effective_debye_length_local()  — central-FD λ_eff
  - Phase 2.4: new multi-ion IC branch in
    `Forward/bv_solver/forms_logc{,_muh}.py:_try_debye_boltzmann_ic*`.
    Triggered when `len(bikerman) > 1`.
    Uses ψ-vs-φ split, linear-Debye Stern matching, multi-ion γ_psi(y)
    from shared-theta closure.
  - Phase 3: driver `scripts/studies/peroxide_window_3sp_parallel_2e_4e_csplus_so4.py`.

Single-counterion ClO₄⁻ legacy code path is byte-equivalent (12/12
debye_boltzmann tests pass on logc + logc_muh).

### Hard rules from CLAUDE.md (non-negotiable)

1. C+D orchestrator (`solve_grid_per_voltage_cold_with_warm_fallback`),
   not Strategy B.
2. `exponent_clip = 100.0` (clip is on `α·n_e·η` AFTER multiplication;
   this is the only PC-trustworthy setting). Lowering this is a
   physics regression — see `docs/clipping_conventions.md`.
3. The IC and the residual must agree about steric saturation
   (composite-ψ + multispecies-γ both seeded). A bikerman IC without
   the matching residual cold-fails on the saturated manifold.
4. Solver convergence window: V_RHE ∈ [-0.5, +1.0] V via C+D
   (production reference: docs/4sp_bikerman_ic_option_2b_results.md).
   Use physical E_eq (R₁=0.68 V, R₂=1.78 V), never E_eq=0.

### Phase 4 result

Anchor smoke at V_RHE = +0.55 V (Ny=80) FAILS for the multi-ion stack.
Cold solve at z=1 (direct from analytic IC) diverges. Orchestrator
falls back to linear-phi + z-ramp; z=0 step ALSO diverges
(`snes_reason=-9 = DIVERGED_LINE_SEARCH`).

Full diagnostic dump:
  StudyResults/fast_realignment_2026-05-08/anchor_smoke/anchor_smoke.json

Key fields from that JSON:
```
"max_phi": 3.34,           # phi at electrode (linear-phi fallback)
"max_u1": +50.35,          # log H₂O₂ blew up (post-Newton-fail state)
"c1_surface_mean": 7.24e21,
"snes_reason": "-9",       # DIVERGED_LINE_SEARCH
"snes_iters": 1,           # diverged on first Newton iter
"picard_iters": 40,
"initializer_fallback": true,
```

The blown-up `u1 = +50` is the post-divergence state on the linear-phi
fallback IC (which the orchestrator falls back to AFTER the multi-ion
analytic IC's z=1 attempt fails). The actual multi-ion IC build is
sane — see Diagnostic 2 below.

### Diagnostic 1: legacy single-counterion + parallel-2e/4e WORKS

Same script with `boltzmann_counterions=[DEFAULT_CLO4_BOLTZMANN_COUNTERION_STERIC]`
and parallel-2e/4e reactions converges:
  - cold success in 33.7 s
  - cd = -1.79e-6 mA/cm²
  - R_2e = -1.79e-6 mA/cm²

So: parallel-2e/4e topology + Stern (C_S=0.10 F/m²) + log_rate +
log_c_muh + log-rate BV all WORK. The regression is multi-ion-specific.

### Diagnostic 2: multi-ion IC build is sane in isolation

`scripts/studies/multi_ion_ic_debug.py` calls
`_try_debye_boltzmann_ic_muh` directly (no orchestrator) at +0.55 V.

Picard returns ok=True at iter 40 with state:
  R_list  = [-5.732e-13, 0.0]    (R_2e tiny, R_4e=0 (k0=0))
  c_s_list = [1.000, 1.000e-04, 0.0833]  (essentially bulk)
  phi_o   = -7.600           (Picard's 1:1-closed-form value)
  psi_D   =  10.87           (Picard's Stern-split with 1:1 c_clo4_b)
  psi_S   =  18.14
  gamma_s =  0.0035

NOTE: Picard's `phi_o = log(H_o / c_clo4_bulk)` is HARDCODED to
single-counterion 1:1 algebra. With c_clo4_bulk = first counterion's
bulk = C_CSPLUS_HAT = 166.58 (Cs⁺), this gives phi_o = log(0.0833/166.58)
= -7.60. That is the WRONG number for multi-ion electroneutrality.

After Picard, my Phase 2.4 multi-ion IC branch OVERRIDES phi_o using
solve_outer_phi_multiion(c_dyn_outer=Picard's c_s_list ≈ bulk):
  phi_o_local ≈ 0.0  (correct — bulk anchor for multi-ion)
  λ_eff      ≈ 1.75e-6 nondim (much smaller than single-ClO4
              λ_D=3.9e-5 because I=0.3 M strongly screens)
  psi_D_local ≈ 1.58 (linear-Debye Stern matching: stern·full_drop·λ_eff
                 / (eps + stern·λ_eff))

Resulting spatial IC fields (from debug script, after assemble):
  u_O2  ∈ [-0.073, 0.0]    (slight surface depletion)
  u_H2O2 ∈ [-9.28, -9.21]  (essentially bulk seed = 1e-4)
  mu_H  ∈ [-2.56, -2.49]   (≈ log(0.0833) = -2.49 everywhere)
  phi   ∈ [0.0, +1.58]     (psi_D_local at electrode → 0 at bulk)

These are physically sensible. log_gamma at electrode ≈ -0.072 (mild,
gamma_psi ≈ 0.93). c_H_at_OHP via mu_H reconstruction
= exp(mu_H - em·z_H·phi) = exp(-2.49 - 1·1·1.58) = exp(-4.07) ≈ 0.017
(c_H/c_H_b ≈ 0.21 — mild depletion, NOT artificial 11-orders-of-mag
collapse like the single-ClO4 case).

### Root cause of Newton divergence

With multi-ion physics correctly giving ψ_D ≈ 1.58, the BV cathodic
rate at +0.55 V is:

  η_R2e_at_surface = phi_applied - phi(0) - E_eq_R2e
                   = 21.4 - 1.58 - 27.05
                   = -7.23  (cathodic, exp factor exp(α·n_e·|η|))

  exp(0.627 · 2 · 7.23) = exp(9.07) ≈ 8700  (well below clip=100)

  R_2e_cathodic = k₀_R2e · c_O · (c_H/c_H_ref)² · exp(...)
                = 1.263e-3 · 1.0 · (0.017/0.0833)² · 8700
                = 1.263e-3 · 1.0 · 0.041 · 8700
                ≈ 0.45  (nondim)

Mass-transport limit (at L_REF=100 µm, D_O2): c_O_b - R/D_O2 = 1 - 0.45 = 0.55.
The "true" SS solution likely sits in this strongly-depleted regime, but Newton
from a nearly-bulk IC (c_O ≈ 1) cannot bridge there robustly when the rate
exponent doesn't have the 11-order-of-magnitude H⁺-depletion safety bound.

### Why the legacy single-ClO₄⁻ stack works

The Picard's `phi_o = log(H_o / c_clo4_bulk)` is exactly 0 when
c_clo4_bulk = c_H_bulk (the legacy 1:1 ClO4 case at pH 4 with both
nondim'd to 0.0833). With phi_o ≈ 0 and Stern+1:1-Bikerman split,
ψ_D ≈ 11 (Stern absorbs ~half of phi_applied=21.4, the rest is in the
diffuse layer).

ψ_D ≈ 11 → c_H/c_H_b = exp(-11) ≈ 1.7e-5 → (c_H/c_H_ref)² ≈ 3e-10.
That single factor BOUNDS the cathodic rate by 11 orders of magnitude
relative to the bulk-evaluated rate. Newton finds a self-consistent
state where R is tiny and c_O ≈ c_O_b. EASY.

But — this works ONLY because the "wrong" c_clo4_bulk = 0.0833 (matched
to H⁺ at pH 4) coincidentally makes phi_o = 0. Try Cs⁺ (c_bulk = 166.58
mol/m³) and the same code gives phi_o = log(0.0833/166.58) = -7.60,
which is mathematically wrong (NOT the multi-ion electroneutrality
solution) AND physically misleading. The resulting IC works in the
single-counterion case only because phi_o ≈ 0 happens to be both right
(by coincidence with bulk-pH electroneutrality) AND helpful (large
ψ_D bounds the rate).

Multi-ion at I=0.3 M is the realistic experiment. There the diffuse
layer is much thinner (λ_eff ≪ λ_D_single_ClO4) and ψ_D is genuinely
small. The BV rate at the production V_RHE grid genuinely is in the
"big and mass-transport-limited" regime. Newton has to find that
state, not be handed an artifact-friendly version of it.

### Relevant file paths and code

Multi-ion machinery:
  - `Forward/bv_solver/multi_ion.py` (NEW, Phase 2.3)
  - `Forward/bv_solver/boltzmann.py:90-265` (multi-counterion closure)
  - `Forward/bv_solver/forms_logc.py:949-1057` (multi-ion IC branch)
  - `Forward/bv_solver/forms_logc_muh.py:1003-1109` (muh multi-ion IC)
  - `Forward/bv_solver/picard_ic.py:1142` (the hardcoded 1:1 phi_o
    `phi_o = math.log(max(H_o, 1e-300) / max(c_clo4_bulk, 1e-300))`
    — currently used by the Picard EVEN in multi-ion mode; my Phase 2.4
    code overrides post-Picard but the Picard's INTERNAL eta_drop and
    psi_D inside the iteration are still computed with the wrong phi_o)

Orchestrator:
  - `Forward/bv_solver/grid_per_voltage.py:319-369` (cold-start with
    z-ramp + warm-fallback). Path B: try direct z=1 from analytic IC;
    if Newton diverges, reset to linear-phi + z-ramp.
  - LINE 350: `set_initial_conditions_logc(...)` — note: this calls the
    LOGC fallback even when formulation is logc_muh. Pre-existing bug
    that the multi-ion path now exposes (linear-phi fallback for muh
    formulation routes through wrong IC builder).

Solver options:
  - SNES_OPTS_CHARGED + linesearch_type=l2, maxlambda=0.3,
    snes_max_it=400, atol=1e-7, rtol=1e-10.

Experimental constants (from Ruggiero §2):
  - C_O2 = 1.2 mol/m³ (ORR-saturated water at pH 4-13)
  - D_O2 = 1.9e-9 m²/s, D_H2O2 = 1.6e-9, D_HP = 9.311e-9
  - C_HP = 0.1 mol/m³ (pH 4)
  - C_CSPLUS = 199.9, C_SO4 = 100.0 mol/m³ (electroneutrality + I=0.3 M)
  - K0_PHYS_R2E = 2.4e-8 m/s (= K0_PHYS_R1, placeholder)
  - K0_PHYS_R4E = 2.4e-8 m/s (PRIOR-SELECTED, same as R2E)
  - α_R2E = 0.627 (Tafel-fit), α_R4E = 0.5 (placeholder)
  - L_REF = 100 µm, V_T = 0.025693 V at 25°C

### Things already ruled out

  - `_try_debye_boltzmann_ic_muh` itself is NOT broken — it returns
    ok=True with sensible state.
  - `picard_outer_loop_general` for parallel topology IS NOT broken
    — Phase 1.2 audit confirmed geometric convergence for parallel-2e/4e.
  - The multi-counterion Bikerman closure in boltzmann.py is correct
    by algebra (single-counterion case byte-equivalent; 19/19 tests
    pass for multi-ion variants).
  - The parallel-2e/4e topology + Stern + log_rate stack DOES converge
    when paired with the legacy single-counterion ClO₄⁻ entry (proven
    in Diagnostic 1).

So the wall is specifically the COUPLING between:
  - Multi-ion's correct ψ_D ≈ 1.58 (small)
  - The BV rate's cathodic exponent at production V_RHE
  - Newton's ability to find the strongly-mass-transport-limited SS
    from any reasonable IC.

## Section 2 — Artifact under review

### Three candidate paths from plan §5

**Path 5b (I-ramp continuation)**:
Ramp ionic strength from low to literature values across pseudo-time
steps. Concretely: scale `C_CSPLUS_HAT, C_SO4_HAT` by α ∈ {0.01, 0.1,
0.5, 1.0} across N continuation steps, with Newton repair at each
step. The idea: at low α the EDL is closer to the single-ClO₄⁻ regime
(thicker diffuse layer, larger ψ_D, friendly H⁺ depletion), and at
each α step Newton has a warm-start from the previous α. Hopefully
the path "low-I large-ψ_D" → "high-I small-ψ_D" stays in a
solver-friendly basin throughout.

  Within fast-realignment scope.
  Costs: ~hours of solver time per V (multiple α per V).
  Risks:
    - The path may not actually be smooth; somewhere between α=0.1 and
      α=1.0 the rate transitions from "tiny" (1:1-friendly) to "0.45"
      (mass-transport-limited) and Newton may still struggle.
    - Need to re-instantiate context per α (because c_bulk_nondim is
      baked into the analytic counterion entries → the form), which
      means warm-start has to copy state across contexts. Not done in
      this codebase yet for analytic-counterion bulk concentrations.

**Path 5g (smarter spatial IC)**:
Replace linear `phi_outer(y)` with `solve_outer_phi_multiion()`
evaluated at multiple y nodes plus interpolation between them. Higher-
fidelity IC closer to the SS solution. Specifically: solve the
multi-ion electroneutrality at y nodes {0, λ_eff, 5·λ_eff, L_REF/2,
L_REF}, with c_dyn_outer(y) interpolated as needed, and build a
piecewise-cubic phi_outer(y).

  Out of fast-realignment scope (1-2 days per the plan).
  Costs: implementation effort + risk that even higher-fidelity IC
  doesn't help if the SS Newton basin is narrow.
  Risks:
    - We don't have evidence that the IC quality is the issue. The IC
      is already physically sensible (Diagnostic 2). Newton diverges
      because the BV rate at the IC is much larger than the SS rate,
      not because the IC is far from a Newton-friendly version of the
      SS in some norm we can refine away.
    - Adding more Newton-internal nonlinearity (cubic-spline-of-
      bisection-output evaluated at each quadrature point) may make
      assembly slower and harder to diagnose.

**Path "Outside the plan" (softplus-bounded BV rate)**:
Add a softplus or similar smooth saturation to the BV rate so that
during Newton iteration the rate is bounded above by a physically
motivated limit (e.g., k_Lm * c_O_b, the mass-transport limit).
Specifically, instead of `R = k₀ · c · exp(...) - k₀ · c · exp(...)`,
use something like
  R = R_lim · tanh( (k₀ · c · exp(...) - k₀ · c · exp(...)) / R_lim )
with R_lim chosen as a multiple of the diffusion-limited current.

  Out of plan, addresses root cause directly, but invasive.
  Risks:
    - Distorts the physical SS unless R_lim is chosen carefully and
      taken to ∞ at convergence (continuation in R_lim).
    - PC trustworthiness implications (CLAUDE.md hard rule 2 explicitly
      forbids modifying the BV exponent clip; a tanh saturation on the
      rate is a different bound but may still trip downstream
      assumptions about clip physics in `docs/clipping_conventions.md`).
    - Have to build it for parallel-2e/4e in both `forms_logc.py` and
      `forms_logc_muh.py`, plus handle log-rate vs concentration-rate
      branches.

### What I haven't done yet but plausibly should

  1. Patch `picard_outer_loop_general` to use multi-ion-aware phi_o
     (not the hardcoded 1:1 `log(H_o/c_clo4_bulk)`). The Picard's
     INTERNAL state is still wrong for multi-ion even though my
     Phase 2.4 IC builder overrides it post-loop. If the Picard's
     own eta_drop and psi_D were correct, the c_s_list it produces
     would also reflect mass-transport limitation, and the IC
     downstream would seed a much-more-depleted O_s and H_o, which
     could be the difference Newton needs.

  2. Pre-relax via a transient. Instead of asking SS Newton to solve
     directly, run a few transient time steps from a benign IC (e.g.,
     bulk-flat) and let the system find its own EDL via diffusion +
     electromigration. Then SS-solve from the relaxed state. The
     existing solver supports transient stepping (dt, t_end set in
     SolverParams).

  3. Smaller Stern coefficient continuation: ramp Stern from a "weaker"
     value (e.g., C_S = 0.01 F/m², which would absorb less of the
     drop and produce larger ψ_D) up to the literature value. This
     would mimic the single-ClO₄⁻ "large ψ_D" situation at the start
     and walk down to the realistic Stern.

  4. Reduce K0_R2e at first, walk up. Same logic as Stern: at very
     small k₀, the BV rate is bounded by k₀ even at full overpotential,
     so Newton has an easy SS. Walk k₀ from 0 to literature.

  5. Combine: cold-start at low V_RHE (e.g., -0.5 V where the Tafel
     direction puts R_2e in anodic direction with strong inhibition
     from c_H2O2 bulk = 1e-4 — actually anodic rate ∝ c_H2O2 which
     is tiny, so net rate is tiny → easy SS), then warm-walk to
     +0.55 V. The C+D orchestrator has warm-walk built in. We just
     need a cold success somewhere.

  6. Hybrid: use the ARTIFACT-BENEFICIAL single-ClO₄⁻ IC as a
     starting state (where ψ_D ≈ 11 → strong H⁺ depletion → Newton-
     friendly), then SWAP to multi-ion residual and let Newton find
     the correct multi-ion SS from this strongly-EDL IC. This relies
     on the "wrong-but-friendly" IC and the "right" residual coupling
     to a basin Newton can navigate.

### Question for GPT

  - Are the three plan §5 paths (5b, 5g, softplus) actually viable?
    Find every hole.
  - Are the 6 alternatives I sketched above viable? Find every hole.
  - Is there a path I'm missing that would be better than any of
    these?
  - Specifically: which path has the highest probability of
    ≥ 15/25 V_RHE converged with non-zero R_2e in the smallest
    number of additional engineering hours?
  - Is "Patch Picard for multi-ion phi_o" (option 1 in my list)
    actually the ROOT cause fix that enables everything else, and
    therefore should land BEFORE any continuation strategy?

I want a recommendation with reasoning, not a vague "try them all".
Prioritize by signal-to-implementation-cost ratio. Be willing to
say "the plan §5 paths are all wrong, here's what's actually
needed" if that's what the algebra says.

Cite specific lines / formulas / code paths. Don't be vague. If you
think my BV rate calculation is wrong (R ≈ 0.45 nondim), say where.

## Section 3 — Critique prompt

You are an adversarial reviewer. Be critical. Be argumentative.
Find every hole: missing steps, wrong algebra, untested assumptions,
edge cases not addressed, implicit dependencies, claims without
evidence, off-by-one errors, sign errors, dimensional errors. Don't
be polite — if something is wrong, say so. Concision over hedging.

For each issue, state:
  - WHAT is wrong (specific, not vague — name the line or symbol)
  - WHY it matters (what breaks downstream if uncorrected)
  - WHAT to do (concrete fix, or what evidence would close the gap)

Number your issues. After all issues, end your response with exactly
one of these lines, no other text after it:

  VERDICT: APPROVED
  VERDICT: ISSUES_REMAIN

Use APPROVED only when there are no issues you would block on.
Minor nitpicks alone do not justify ISSUES_REMAIN — call them out
but still verdict APPROVED. Use ISSUES_REMAIN whenever any of your
issues are genuinely blocking.

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_5_FIM_DEFINITIVE_NEXT_ANODIC.md:35:R2 has E_eq,2 = 1.78 V vs RHE. The cathodic BV exponent `α_2 · n_e · η_2 / V_T = 0.5 · 2 · (-73 to -62) ≈ -73 to -62`, far past the clip `±50`. docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_5_FIM_DEFINITIVE_NEXT_ANODIC.md:83:4. **Should we drop the BV exponent clip entirely?** The clip is currently `±50` on `α n_e η / V_T`. Removing it means `exp(73)` and bigger appears in the residual at high η. With double-precision floats we have ~700 of overhead before overflow, so `exp(73) ≈ 5e31` is fine numerically. The clip was added to prevent SNES from diverging when concentrations are tiny (because the rate `k0 · exp(huge) · c_tiny` may still be moderate but its derivative w.r.t. c_tiny is enormous). Maybe with a positivity-preserving discretization, we don't need the clip and can solve directly?
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_5_FIM_DEFINITIVE_NEXT_ANODIC.md:85:5. **Inverse-problem-side question:** if we *did* succeed at V_RHE = 1.0+ V and got direct R2 sensitivity, the data would be very strong — likely no longer ridge-limited at all. Is there value in *first* validating the full inverse pipeline by running at synthetic high-V data (i.e., having a hypothetical solver hand us cd/pc curves at V_RHE up to 1.5 V) before investing in the actual numerical work? This would de-risk the pipeline and let us estimate what accuracy improvement to expect from the new solver.

docs/Next Steps After Basin Geometry.md:6:Read HANDOFF_10 as the current state. Do not re-run LM, L-BFGS-B tuning, or log(k0) Tikhonov at sigma=log(3)/log(10). Those routes have already shown that the single-experiment CD+PC inverse has multi-basin Tafel-ridge geometry that ordinary optimizers and literature-defensible priors do not fix. Implement the next path in this order: (1) cheap closure diagnostics on the single-experiment basin geometry, (2) anchored Tafel-coordinate parameterization, (3) multi-experiment FIM design screening with bulk O2 variation first, H2O2-fed R2 isolation second, and L_ref/rotation variation third, and (4) full clean-data inverse only for designs whose FIM actually rotates/lifts the remaining weak log_k0 direction. Do not run noisy seeds until clean-data multi-experiment recovery works from multiple initializations.

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_4_PRECISION_AND_NEXT.md:26:At tight precision (`rel_tol=1e-6`, 5 consec convergence), the residual landscape is more rugged because tiny iteration-history-dependent variations in the converged state become visible. The optimizer can no longer slide along the ridge cleanly because it now sees that "moving along the ridge" produces small but nonzero residuals. So it moves *off* the ridge in the k0_1 direction, recovering k0_1 substantially closer to TRUE — but α_1 and k0_2 drift to compensate, and the final cost stays large because the new "valley" the optimizer settles in is also non-true.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_4_PRECISION_AND_NEXT.md:30:**Precision shifts which wrong-point the optimizer lands at, not whether it finds TRUE.** It's not numerical — the FIM cond ~ 1e11 ridge is structural. Tight precision exposed previously-buried information about k0_1, but α and k0_2 followed the (rotated) ridge to compensate.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_4_PRECISION_AND_NEXT.md:32:This rules out "tighter solver = solve k0" as a viable single-experiment path. It also reinforces the multi-experiment framing — the ridge has to be *bent*, not just *exposed at higher resolution*.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_4_PRECISION_AND_NEXT.md:47:Per-design metrics: σ_min(S_white), cond(F), smallest eigenvector of F, *and* the inner product of that eigvec with the canonical ridge direction `[+1, 0, 0.02, 0]` (per breakthrough analysis: 1% α shift ↔ 47% k0 shift on the canonical ridge). If the weak eigvec rotates *away* from this canonical direction in a multi-experiment design, that's quantitative proof the ridge has been broken.

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:191:**Diagnosis of why "log-c didn't work" before:** R2 has E_eq,2 = 1.78 V, so η_2 = φ_applied - E_eq,2 is very negative everywhere in the operating window. With BV exponent clip at ±50, `exp(-α n_e η_2)` saturates at exp(50) ≈ 5e21 across the full V range. Combined with the c_surf concentration floor (1e-12), the spurious R2 sink rate is ≈ k0_2 · exp(50) · (c_H+/c_ref)² · 1e-12 ≈ 0.5 per unit time. When c_H2O2 → 0 at anodic V (R1 produces almost no H2O2), this spurious sink has nothing to balance and Newton finds a "solution" with c_H2O2 ≈ -0.69. CG1 oscillation around the near-zero state amplifies it.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:197:4. **Voltage range V_RHE ∈ [-0.10, +0.30] V** (the onset region). Outside this, log-c without warm-starting fails (V = -0.30 has no good IC; V ≥ +0.40 has H2O2 runaway from BV mismatch).
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:198:5. **Tikhonov regularization on log k0:** J_total = J_data + λ · (log k0 - log k0_prior)² with λ = 0.01.

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:228:**The fundamental issue:** the BV form `r = k0 · exp(-α n_e η / V_T)` has a structural near-degeneracy. A change in k0 can be absorbed by a change in α through the identity `log r = log k0 + (-α n_e η / V_T)`. Over a narrow η range (the onset is only ~150 mV wide), the Hessian has a near-zero eigenvalue along the direction d(log k0)/d(α) = -n_e η_center / V_T ≈ -50, exactly matching the empirically observed ridge slope.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:231:- **Independent k0 measurement** (Tafel analysis on a subset of data, EIS exchange current measurement, literature value) → Tikhonov prior.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:232:- **Multi-experiment fitting** with varying L_ref (rotation rate), c_O2_bulk, T, or pH. k0 is intrinsic; α is intrinsic; the diffusion-limited current scales differently. Joint fit breaks the ridge.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:233:- **Multi-observable** — simultaneously fit cd(V) and the peroxide selectivity PC(V)/CD(V). PC depends on k0_2/k0_1 ratio differently than total CD does. v13 used this and got the best k0 recovery.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:235:- **Mass-transport-coupled features** — the H+ depletion feedback (which makes the surface c_H+ shift with k0) introduces some k0 dependence into the transport-limited current. Currently weak signal because c_H+ is buffered by ClO4- electroneutrality.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:241:**Primary question: what could make k0 (especially k0_2) identifiable in this system, given:**

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:244:- We can extend even further with log-c + seeded H2O2 (V_RHE up to ~+0.30 cleanly) but with constraints on what can be tested.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:250:1. **Physics-side ideas:** Are there ORR-specific tricks people in electrochemistry use to break the (k0, α) ridge that we should be using? (Tafel intercept extrapolation, Koutecký–Levich, EIS-derived j_0 priors, Tafel slope from Allen–Hickling plot, etc.) Which of these can be turned into either an extra term in J or an extra residual in a multi-experiment fit?
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:258:5. **Tikhonov design:** Our λ = 0.01 was eyeballed. L-curve or discrepancy principle would let us pick it from the data. But more fundamentally — what's the right space to regularize in? log k0 is what we're using. Should we regularize the Tafel intercept j_0 = k0 · n_e F · c_bulk instead (more physical)? Should the regularizer be anisotropic (loose along the ridge direction, tight perpendicular)?
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:260:6. **Bayesian / MCMC alternative:** Profile likelihood says (k0, α) has a long thin ridge. A flat prior on α with a weakly-informative prior on log k0 (centered on literature with 10× width) would give a posterior whose maximum is well-defined and whose marginals quantify uncertainty honestly. Is this a more defensible approach for a publication than point estimation + Tikhonov?
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:262:7. **Surrogate hybrid:** v13's approach of "cheap surrogate global search → PDE refinement" got 4–5% k0 error in the cathodic region. Can we revive this with a surrogate trained over the working window of the new 3sp+Boltzmann+log-c forward model, then use Tikhonov refinement on the PDE? The surrogate provides the prior the Tikhonov term needs.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md:266:9. **Ill-posedness as a feature:** if k0 is genuinely non-identifiable from a single I–V curve at 2% noise, and we can prove this via Fisher information, then the publishable story might shift from "we recover k0" to "we quantify what is and isn't recoverable, and provide a Bayesian interval for k0." Does that reframing hold up given how these papers usually look?

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_3_LSQ_RIDGE_RESULT.md:92:2. **Numerical conditioning (TRF behavior):** cond ≈ 1e11 in F-space means cond ≈ 3e5 in residual-space, which exceeds the relative precision of CG1+Newton forward solves (~1e-6 best case). So while the data carries the information, no Jacobian-based optimizer running on standard double-precision forward solves can extract k0 reliably from a single-experiment fit.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_3_LSQ_RIDGE_RESULT.md:94:3. **What's actually recoverable from disk+peroxide:** **α is robustly recoverable** — TRF got both α's within 5% of TRUE without any prior. docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:5:In the prior handoff (`CHATGPT_HANDOFF.md`) you correctly pointed out that the 3-species + Boltzmann ClO4⁻ background solver still has both R1 and R2 reactions and therefore can compute peroxide current from `r1 - r2` directly. You hypothesized that adding peroxide current as a second observable to the joint inverse objective would break the (k0, α) ridge degeneracy that has been blocking k0 identifiability — because disk current sees `r1 + r2` while peroxide sees `r1 - r2`, providing independent constraints on the partitioning between R1 and R2.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:11:Forward physics: the breakthrough recipe from `k0_inference_status.md` exactly as documented:
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:16:- Working voltage window V_RHE ∈ {-0.10, 0.00, +0.10, +0.15, +0.20} V (5 points; dropped V=+0.25 because at +20% offset on all 4 params it falls past the convergence cliff)
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:21:- 4 free parameters: log(k0_1), log(k0_2), α_1, α_2

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:47:**Pattern is unambiguous:** both k0's stayed within 2% of their +20% init while both α's moved 25% — overshooting TRUE by ~5% in the same direction. This is the (k0, α) ridge degeneracy expressed mechanistically: the optimizer descends J by sliding α downward to compensate for inflated k0, finding a local minimum *on the ridge* rather than at TRUE.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:49:That this happens at clean data — where the global minimum J = 0 sits exactly at TRUE — confirms the optimizer found a genuine stationary point. Per the breakthrough script's analysis, the ridge has slope d(log k0)/dα ≈ -47, so when ∂J/∂α = 0 at the ridge bottom, ∂J/∂log k0 = 0 there too. The ridge is in (log k0_1, α_1, log k0_2, α_2) space; both reactions exhibit it.

docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:60:Noise masks the α gradient signal further (only α_2 made meaningful progress under noise). Clean data shows the full extent of α movement that the joint observable enables — but k0 still doesn't move in either case.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:64:R2 has E_eq,2 = 1.78 V vs RHE. At every voltage in our working window V_RHE ∈ [-0.10, +0.20] V, the R2 overpotential η_2 = V - E_eq,2 ∈ [-1.88, -1.58] V — extremely cathodic. With α_2 = 0.5, n_e = 2, V_T = 25.69 mV, the R2 BV exponent is α_2·n_e·η_2/V_T ∈ [-73, -62]. The exponent clip at ±50 saturates this to exp(50) for *every voltage* in the window.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:66:So R2's rate at the electrode is `r_2 = k0_2 · exp(50) · (c_H+/c_ref)² · c_H2O2_surf`. The exponential saturation means **r_2 depends only on c_H2O2_surf and k0_2 multiplicatively at every voltage in our window** — there is no voltage-dependent BV "shape" information to disentangle k0_2 from α_2 (or to disentangle R1 contributions from R2 contributions).
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:70:The premise that "peroxide carries `r_1 - r_2` info that disk doesn't" only holds when both reactions are operating in their kinetic (non-saturated) regimes. In our current window, R2 is saturated everywhere. Disk current sees k0_1 mainly (since r_2 << r_1 in absolute terms), and peroxide also sees k0_1 mainly (same reason). The two observables are nearly redundant.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:72:**This explains the result quantitatively:** peroxide adds essentially zero new information about k0_2, so the inverse remains underdetermined exactly where v17 originally found it.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:76:The peroxide-as-second-observable strategy *would* work if we could move R2 out of its saturated regime — i.e., access voltages closer to E_eq,2 = 1.78 V. But the solver doesn't converge anywhere near that anodic regime (the convergence cliff is around V_RHE ≈ +0.30 V even in log-c+Boltzmann). So under the current forward model, peroxide can't break the ridge regardless of objective weighting or optimizer choice.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:80:1. **Tikhonov + peroxide combined** (low effort, ~1 hour). The breakthrough script (`v18_logc_regularized.py`) already shows Tikhonov on log(k0) recovers k0_1 to <1% in 2D. Adding peroxide as a second observable to the *same* objective might tighten that result and/or extend it cleanly to 4 params. The ridge isn't broken by peroxide alone, but combined with a weak prior, peroxide + Tikhonov could give better recovery than Tikhonov alone.
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:82:2. **Multi-experiment fitting** (medium effort, ~1 week). Vary L_ref (rotation rate) or c_O2_bulk between experiments. The diffusion-limited current scales as D · c_bulk / L_ref while the BV-controlled regime depends on k0 · c_surf — they shift differently with the experimental knob. Joint fitting across 2-3 experiments breaks the ridge from a *different* physical principle than peroxide. This is standard practice in electrochemistry (Koutecký-Levich analysis is essentially this).
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:90:2. **Would extending the voltage window to access *less* anodic R2 conditions help?** R2's E_eq is so high (1.78 V) that we'd need V_RHE near or above 1.78 V to get η_2 in the kinetic regime — but we can't push the forward solver past +0.30 V in any tested formulation. Is there a clever observable construction that exposes R2 kinetics from data taken in the saturated regime?
docs/CHATGPT_HANDOFF_2_PEROXIDE_RESULT.md:94:4. **Is there a dimensionally-different observable we're missing?** E.g., DC vs AC, time-resolved transient response vs steady-state, EIS spectrum at specific frequencies. We're currently only fitting steady-state I-V; expanding to transient or frequency-domain might add k0 information that disentangles from α.

     1	"""Multi-ion analytic-counterion machinery for the fast-realignment plan.
     2	
     3	Single source of truth for the multi-ion shared-theta closure used by
     4	both the Picard outer loop (electroneutrality at the outer-region edge)
     5	and the spatial IC seed (forms_logc[_muh].py).  Mirrors the
     6	single-counterion ``compute_surface_gamma`` / GC-Stern split helpers in
     7	``picard_ic.py`` but generalizes to N steric counterions sharing one
     8	denominator.
     9	
    10	Closure (plan §2.1):
    11	
    12	    For each analytic ion k (steric):
    13	      c_k(φ) = c_b_k · exp(-z_k·φ) · (1 - A_dyn(φ))
    14	                   / (θ_b + Σ_k' a_k' · c_b_k' · exp(-z_k'·φ))
    15	
    16	    with A_dyn(φ) = Σ_dyn a_i · c_i_dyn(φ)
    17	         θ_b      = 1 - A_dyn_bulk - Σ_k a_k · c_b_k
    18	
    19	The denominator is the same for every steric ion (shared theta); no
    20	coupled local NL solve needed.
    21	
    22	Used by:
    23	  - ``picard_outer_loop_general`` (post-loop reconstruction at the
    24	    OHP edge): solves outer-region phi_o via bisection on the
    25	    multi-ion electroneutrality residual; computes multispecies γ_s
    26	    at OHP; computes local λ_eff for the linear-Debye Stern split.
    27	  - ``forms_logc[_muh].py:_try_debye_boltzmann_ic*`` (spatial IC):
    28	    interpolates each species onto the multi-ion ψ-vs-φ split with
    29	    the shared-theta packing factor.
    30	"""
    31	from __future__ import annotations
    32	
    33	import math
    34	from dataclasses import dataclass, field
    35	from typing import Any
    36	
    37	
    38	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    39	# Numerical primitives
    40	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    41	
    42	def _safe_exp(x: float, *, cap: float = 700.0) -> float:
    43	    """``math.exp`` with a symmetric cap so multi-ion bisections can't
    44	    overflow when ψ wanders far during root-finding.
    45	
    46	    Mirrors ``picard_ic._safe_exp`` to keep the multi-ion module
    47	    standalone (no import cycle).
    48	    """
    49	    if x > cap:
    50	        return math.exp(cap)
    51	    if x < -cap:
    52	        return math.exp(-cap)
    53	    return math.exp(x)

    56	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    57	# CounterionConfig
    58	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    59	
    60	@dataclass(frozen=True)
    61	class CounterionConfig:
    62	    """Per-counterion immutable record consumed by the multi-ion helpers.
    63	
    64	    Mirrors the dict shape produced by
    65	    ``DEFAULT_CSPLUS_BOLTZMANN_COUNTERION_STERIC`` etc., but typed and
    66	    frozen.  The ctx builder accepts either dict entries or instances of
    67	    this class — dicts are normalised into instances at the boundary.
    68	    """
    69	    z: int
    70	    c_bulk_nondim: float
    71	    a_nondim: float
    72	    steric_mode: str = "ideal"      # "ideal" | "bikerman"
    73	    phi_clamp: float = 50.0
    74	    label: str = ""
    75	
    76	
    77	def _normalize_entry(entry: Any) -> dict:
    78	    """Coerce a CounterionConfig OR dict to a flat dict with all keys.
    79	
    80	    Preserves the dict shape downstream callers (boltzmann.py) expect.
    81	    """
    82	    if isinstance(entry, CounterionConfig):
    83	        return {
    84	            "z": int(entry.z),
    85	            "c_bulk_nondim": float(entry.c_bulk_nondim),
    86	            "a_nondim": float(entry.a_nondim),
    87	            "steric_mode": str(entry.steric_mode),
    88	            "phi_clamp": float(entry.phi_clamp),
    89	            "label": str(entry.label),
    90	        }
    91	    if isinstance(entry, dict):
    92	        return {
    93	            "z": int(entry["z"]),
    94	            "c_bulk_nondim": float(entry["c_bulk_nondim"]),
    95	            "a_nondim": float(entry.get("a_nondim", 0.0)),
    96	            "steric_mode": str(entry.get("steric_mode", "ideal")),
    97	            "phi_clamp": float(entry.get("phi_clamp", 50.0)),
    98	            "label": str(entry.get("label", "")),
    99	        }
   100	    raise TypeError(
   101	        f"_normalize_entry: expected CounterionConfig or dict, got {type(entry)!r}"
   102	    )
   103	
   104	
   105	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   106	# Counterion context builder (single producer of theta_b)
   107	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   108	
   109	def build_counterion_ctx(
   110	    counterions: list,
   111	    a_dyn: list[float],
   112	    c_dyn_bulk: list[float],
   113	    z_dyn: list[int],
   114	) -> dict:
   115	    """Build the canonical multi-ion counterion context.
   116	
   117	    Single producer of ``theta_b``; downstream readers MUST consume it
   118	    from this ctx rather than recomputing from raw inputs (avoids
   119	    sign / inclusion drift between Picard and the residual side).
   120	
   121	    Parameters
   122	    ----------
   123	    counterions:
   124	        Sequence of CounterionConfig OR raw config dicts (the latter
   125	        as produced by ``DEFAULT_CSPLUS_BOLTZMANN_COUNTERION_STERIC``
   126	        etc.).  Mixed allowed.
   127	    a_dyn, c_dyn_bulk, z_dyn:
   128	        Per dynamic species, length n_dyn.
   129	
   130	    Returns
   131	    -------
   132	    dict with keys:
   133	        - ``ions``: list of normalised counterion dicts
   134	        - ``z_dyn``, ``c_dyn_bulk``, ``a_dyn``: passthrough copies
   135	        - ``theta_b``: bulk packing fraction (1 - A_dyn_bulk - Σ a_k c_b_k)
   136	    """
   137	    if not counterions:
   138	        return {
   139	            "ions": [], "z_dyn": list(z_dyn),
   140	            "c_dyn_bulk": [float(c) for c in c_dyn_bulk],
   141	            "a_dyn": [float(a) for a in a_dyn],
   142	            "theta_b": 1.0 - sum(a * c for a, c in zip(a_dyn, c_dyn_bulk)),
   143	        }
   144	    ions = [_normalize_entry(e) for e in counterions]
   145	    A_dyn_bulk = sum(a * c for a, c in zip(a_dyn, c_dyn_bulk))
   146	    A_an_bulk = sum(
   147	        ion["a_nondim"] * ion["c_bulk_nondim"]
   148	        for ion in ions if ion["steric_mode"] == "bikerman"
   149	    )
   150	    theta_b = 1.0 - A_dyn_bulk - A_an_bulk
   151	    if theta_b <= 0.0:
   152	        bm_str = ", ".join(
   153	            f"{ion.get('label','?')}: a={ion['a_nondim']:.4g}*c_b={ion['c_bulk_nondim']:.4g}"
   154	            for ion in ions if ion["steric_mode"] == "bikerman"
   155	        )
   156	        raise ValueError(
   157	            f"build_counterion_ctx: theta_b <= 0 (got {theta_b:.6g}) — "
   158	            f"sum(a_k*c_b_k) for steric counterions = {A_an_bulk:.6g}; "
   159	            f"A_dyn_bulk = {A_dyn_bulk:.6g}; bikerman entries: [{bm_str}]; "
   160	            f"reduce dynamic-species packing or per-ion a_nondim/c_bulk_nondim."
   161	        )
   162	    return {
   163	        "ions": ions,
   164	        "z_dyn": [int(z) for z in z_dyn],
   165	        "c_dyn_bulk": [float(c) for c in c_dyn_bulk],
   166	        "a_dyn": [float(a) for a in a_dyn],
   167	        "theta_b": float(theta_b),
   168	    }
   169	
   170	
   171	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   172	# Outer-region phi solve
   173	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   174	
   175	def _ck_at_phi(*, ion: dict, phi: float, A_dyn_local: float,
   176	               theta_b: float, ions: list, denom_cache: float | None = None) -> float:
   177	    """Multi-steric closure single-ion concentration at potential ``phi``.
   178	
   179	    Matches ``boltzmann.build_steric_boltzmann_expressions`` UFL algebra
   180	    (ideal ions degenerate to ``c_b · exp(-z·phi)``; bikerman uses the
   181	    shared-theta closure).  ``denom_cache`` lets the caller compute the
   182	    shared denominator once and reuse it across all ions.
   183	    """
   184	    z = float(ion["z"])
   185	    c_b = float(ion["c_bulk_nondim"])
   186	    if ion.get("steric_mode", "ideal") != "bikerman":
   187	        return c_b * _safe_exp(-z * phi)
   188	    if denom_cache is None:
   189	        denom_cache = theta_b + sum(
   190	            ip["a_nondim"] * ip["c_bulk_nondim"] * _safe_exp(-ip["z"] * phi)
   191	            for ip in ions if ip.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"
   192	        )
   193	    return c_b * _safe_exp(-z * phi) * max(1.0 - A_dyn_local, 1e-12) / max(denom_cache, 1e-300)
   194	
   195	
   196	def _electroneutrality_residual(
   197	    *, phi: float, ctx: dict, c_dyn: list[float],
   198	) -> float:
   199	    """ρ_total(phi) = Σ z_dyn·c_dyn + Σ z_an·c_an(phi).
   200	
   201	    Both sums are evaluated at the *outer-region* edge (NOT bulk):
   202	    the Picard yields ``c_dyn = [O_s, P_s, H_o]`` at the OHP-side edge
   203	    and the analytic ions equilibrate against that local A_dyn rather
   204	    than the bulk A_dyn_bulk (the Boltzmann profile is local).
   205	    """
   206	    z_dyn = ctx["z_dyn"]
   207	    a_dyn = ctx["a_dyn"]
   208	    ions = ctx["ions"]
   209	    theta_b = ctx["theta_b"]
   210	    A_dyn_local = sum(a * c for a, c in zip(a_dyn, c_dyn))
   211	    denom = theta_b + sum(
   212	        ion["a_nondim"] * ion["c_bulk_nondim"] * _safe_exp(-ion["z"] * phi)
   213	        for ion in ions if ion.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"
   214	    )
   215	    rho_dyn = sum(z * c for z, c in zip(z_dyn, c_dyn))
   216	    rho_an = sum(
   217	        float(ion["z"]) * _ck_at_phi(
   218	            ion=ion, phi=phi, A_dyn_local=A_dyn_local,
   219	            theta_b=theta_b, ions=ions, denom_cache=denom,
   220	        ) for ion in ions
   221	    )
   222	    return rho_dyn + rho_an
   223

   256	
   257	    Returns

   260	        Outer-region equilibrium potential (nondim).

   989	    psi_gc = fd.Constant(2.0) * fd.ln(
   990	        (fd.Constant(1.0) + arg_safe) / (fd.Constant(1.0) - arg_safe)
   991	    )
   992	
   993	    O_outer = fd.Constant(O_s) + (fd.Constant(O_b) - fd.Constant(O_s)) * y
   994	    P_outer = fd.max_value(
   995	        fd.Constant(P_s) + (fd.Constant(P_b) - fd.Constant(P_s)) * y,
   996	        fd.Constant(P_FLOOR),
   997	    )
   998	    H_outer = fd.max_value(
   999	        fd.Constant(H_o) + (fd.Constant(H_b) - fd.Constant(H_o)) * y,
  1000	        fd.Constant(1e-300),
  1001	    )
  1002	
  1003	    # ----- Multi-ion IC branch (plan §2.4) -------------------------------
  1004	    # When 2+ bikerman counterions are configured (Cs⁺ + SO₄²⁻ etc.), the
  1005	    # 1:1 BKSA composite-psi closure no longer applies; use the multi-ion
  1006	    # shared-theta machinery in ``Forward.bv_solver.multi_ion``.  Mirrors
  1007	    # forms_logc.py multi-ion branch with the muh-specific
  1008	    # ``mu_H = u_H + em*z_H*phi`` accumulation for the proton.
  1009	    bikerman_entries_in_counterions = [
  1010	        e for e in counterions
  1011	        if e.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"
  1012	    ]
  1013	    multi_ion_mode = len(bikerman_entries_in_counterions) > 1
  1014	    if multi_ion_mode:
  1015	        from .multi_ion import (
  1016	            build_counterion_ctx, solve_outer_phi_multiion,
  1017	            effective_debye_length_local,
  1018	        )
  1019	        a_vals_full_mion = list(solver_params[6])
  1020	        a_dyn_for_ctx = [float(v) for v in a_vals_full_mion[:n]]
  1021	        c_dyn_bulk_for_ctx = [float(O_b), float(P_b), float(H_b)]
  1022	        z_dyn_for_ctx = [int(v) for v in z_vals_full[:n]]
  1023	        ctx_mion = build_counterion_ctx(
  1024	            counterions=counterions,
  1025	            a_dyn=a_dyn_for_ctx,
  1026	            c_dyn_bulk=c_dyn_bulk_for_ctx,
  1027	            z_dyn=z_dyn_for_ctx,
  1028	        )
  1029	        c_dyn_outer_at_ohp = [float(O_s), float(P_s), float(H_o)]
  1030	        try:
  1031	            phi_o_local = solve_outer_phi_multiion(
  1032	                ctx=ctx_mion, c_dyn_outer=c_dyn_outer_at_ohp,
  1033	            )
  1034	        except ValueError as e:
  1035	            return False, f"multi_ion_phi_o_solve_failed: {e}", picard_iters
  1036	        lambda_eff = effective_debye_length_local(
  1037	            phi_o=phi_o_local, ctx=ctx_mion,
  1038	            c_dyn_outer=c_dyn_outer_at_ohp,
  1039	            poisson_coeff=poisson_coefficient,
  1040	        )
  1041	        full_drop = float(phi_applied_model) - phi_o_local
  1042	        if use_stern_at_ic:
  1043	            stern_coeff_val = float(stern_capacitance_model)
  1044	            psi_D_local = (
  1045	                stern_coeff_val * full_drop * lambda_eff
  1046	                / (poisson_coefficient + stern_coeff_val * lambda_eff)
  1047	            )
  1048	        else:
  1049	            psi_D_local = full_drop
  1050	
  1051	        psi = fd.Constant(psi_D_local) * fd.exp(-y / fd.Constant(lambda_eff))
  1052	        phi_outer = fd.Constant(phi_o_local) * (
  1053	            fd.Constant(1.0) - fd.min_value(y, fd.Constant(1.0))
  1054	        )
  1055	        phi_init_expr = phi_outer + psi
  1056	
  1057	        A_dyn_outer = sum(
  1058	            a * c for a, c in zip(a_dyn_for_ctx, c_dyn_outer_at_ohp)
  1059	        )
  1060	        denom_outer = ctx_mion["theta_b"] + sum(
  1061	            ion["a_nondim"] * ion["c_bulk_nondim"]
  1062	            * math.exp(-ion["z"] * phi_o_local)
  1063	            for ion in ctx_mion["ions"]
  1064	            if ion.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"
  1065	        )
  1066	        theta_outer_const = max(
  1067	            (1.0 - A_dyn_outer) * ctx_mion["theta_b"] / max(denom_outer, 1e-300),
  1068	            1e-30,
  1069	        )
  1070	        c_outer_y_list = [O_outer, P_outer, H_outer]
  1071	        A_dyn_y = sum(
  1072	            fd.Constant(a) * c_y for a, c_y in zip(a_dyn_for_ctx, c_outer_y_list)
  1073	        )
  1074	        denom_y = fd.Constant(ctx_mion["theta_b"]) + sum(
  1075	            fd.Constant(ion["a_nondim"] * ion["c_bulk_nondim"])
  1076	            * fd.exp(fd.Constant(-float(ion["z"])) * (phi_outer + psi))
  1077	            for ion in ctx_mion["ions"]
  1078	            if ion.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"
  1079	        )
  1080	        theta_y = (
  1081	            (fd.Constant(1.0) - A_dyn_y)
  1082	            * fd.Constant(ctx_mion["theta_b"]) / denom_y
  1083	        )
  1084	        gamma_psi = theta_y / fd.Constant(theta_outer_const)
  1085	        log_gamma = fd.ln(fd.max_value(gamma_psi, fd.Constant(1e-30)))
  1086	
  1087	        # Spatial IC for each species — muh formulation stores H+ as
  1088	        # mu_H = u_H + em*z_H*phi (with em*z_H=1, the -psi shift in u_H
  1089	        # cancels the +psi in phi inside mu_H, leaving log_gamma propagated).
  1090	        z_dyn_int = [int(v) for v in z_vals_full[:n]]
  1091	        for i in range(n):
  1092	            log_c_outer_i = fd.ln(c_outer_y_list[i])
  1093	            u_i_init = (
  1094	                log_c_outer_i
  1095	                - fd.Constant(float(z_dyn_int[i])) * psi
  1096	                + log_gamma
  1097	            )
  1098	            if i == mu_h_idx:
  1099	                # H+ stored as mu_H = u_H + em*z_H*phi.
  1100	                mu_h_init = (
  1101	                    u_i_init
  1102	                    + fd.Constant(em * z_h_val) * phi_init_expr
  1103	                )
  1104	                U_prev.sub(i).interpolate(mu_h_init)
  1105	            else:
  1106	                U_prev.sub(i).interpolate(u_i_init)
  1107	        U_prev.sub(n).interpolate(phi_init_expr)
  1108	        ctx["U"].assign(U_prev)
  1109	        return True, "", picard_iters
  1110	
  1111	    # Bikerman-consistent IC paths (synthesised 4sp ClO4-, or explicit
  1112	    # ``boltzmann_counterions=[{steric_mode='bikerman', ...}]``).  Mirrors
  1113	    # forms_logc.py:_try_debye_boltzmann_ic; the only muh-specific bit is
  1114	    # the proton stored as mu_H = u_H + em*z_H*phi (psi cancels with em*z_H = 1,
  1115	    # log_gamma propagates through u_H into mu_H).
  1116	    # ``apply_bikerman_ic`` was already computed above.
  1117	    if apply_bikerman_ic:
  1118	        a_vals_full = list(solver_params[6])
  1119	        a_h = float(a_vals_full[2])
  1120	        if synthesised_4sp_counterion:
  1121	            a_cl = float(a_vals_full[3])
  1122	            c_cl_anchor = H_outer
  1123	        else:
  1124	            bikerman_entry = next(
  1125	                e for e in counterions
  1126	                if e.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"
  1127	            )
  1128	            a_cl = float(bikerman_entry["a_nondim"])
  1129	            c_cl_anchor = fd.Constant(c_clo4_bulk)
  1130	
  1131	        # Composite psi (BKSA matched-asymptotic): saturated zone +
  1132	        # outer exponential decay.  See forms_logc.py for the full
  1133	        # comment block.
  1134	        nu_charged = 2.0 * a_cl * c_clo4_bulk
  1135	        psi_d_abs = abs(float(psi_D))

   260	        Outer-region equilibrium potential (nondim).
   261	
   262	    Raises
   263	    ------
   264	    ValueError
   265	        If the bracket doesn't contain a root after expansion.
   266	    """
   267	    a_low, a_high = float(bracket[0]), float(bracket[1])
   268	    f_low = _electroneutrality_residual(phi=a_low, ctx=ctx, c_dyn=c_dyn_outer)
   269	    f_high = _electroneutrality_residual(phi=a_high, ctx=ctx, c_dyn=c_dyn_outer)
   270	    # Bracket-expansion: try doubling out to ±200 if the initial bracket
   271	    # has the same sign at both ends.
   272	    expand_iters = 0
   273	    while f_low * f_high > 0.0 and expand_iters < 8:
   274	        a_low *= 2.0
   275	        a_high *= 2.0
   276	        f_low = _electroneutrality_residual(phi=a_low, ctx=ctx, c_dyn=c_dyn_outer)
   277	        f_high = _electroneutrality_residual(phi=a_high, ctx=ctx, c_dyn=c_dyn_outer)
   278	        expand_iters += 1
   279	    if f_low * f_high > 0.0:
   280	        raise ValueError(
   281	            f"solve_outer_phi_multiion: bracket [{a_low}, {a_high}] does not "
   282	            f"contain a root (residual signs match: f_low={f_low:.3g}, "
   283	            f"f_high={f_high:.3g}); ctx ions={ctx['ions']!r}, "
   284	            f"c_dyn_outer={c_dyn_outer}"
   285	        )
   286	    for _ in range(max_iter):
   287	        mid = 0.5 * (a_low + a_high)
   288	        f_mid = _electroneutrality_residual(phi=mid, ctx=ctx, c_dyn=c_dyn_outer)
   289	        if abs(f_mid) < tol:
   290	            return mid
   291	        if f_low * f_mid <= 0.0:
   292	            a_high = mid
   293	            f_high = f_mid
   294	        else:
   295	            a_low = mid
   296	            f_low = f_mid
   297	    return 0.5 * (a_low + a_high)

   299	
   300	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   301	# Multispecies surface gamma at OHP
   302	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   303	
   304	def compute_surface_gamma_multiion(
   305	    *,
   306	    H_o: float,
   307	    psi_D: float,
   308	    a_h: float,
   309	    ions: list[dict],
   310	) -> float:
   311	    """Multispecies γ_s at the OHP using outer-region anchors.
   312	
   313	    Generalizes ``picard_ic.compute_surface_gamma`` (which is hard-coded
   314	    to one cation H⁺ + one anion ClO₄⁻ at bulk concentration) to N steric
   315	    ions with their *outer-region* (NOT bulk) concentrations:
   316	
   317	        γ_s = 1 / [
   318	                 1 + a_H · H_o · (e^{-ψ_D} - 1)
   319	                 + Σ_k a_k · c_k_outer · (e^{-z_k·ψ_D} - 1)
   320	            ]
   321	
   322	    where ``ions[k]`` MUST carry a ``"c_outer"`` key with the
   323	    OHP-side outer-region concentration (the multi-ion shared-theta
   324	    closure evaluated at the Picard's ``phi_o``).  For counterions in
   325	    "ideal" mode ``c_outer = c_bulk · exp(-z·phi_o)`` per the standard
   326	    Boltzmann.
   327	
   328	    With ``a_H = 0`` and no steric ions the function returns 1.0.
   329	    """
   330	    if a_h == 0.0 and not ions:
   331	        return 1.0
   332	    denom = 1.0 + a_h * H_o * (_safe_exp(-psi_D) - 1.0)
   333	    for ion in ions:
   334	        denom += float(ion["a_nondim"]) * float(ion["c_outer"]) * (
   335	            _safe_exp(-float(ion["z"]) * psi_D) - 1.0
   336	        )
   337	    if not math.isfinite(denom) or denom <= 0.0:
   338	        return 1e-300
   339	    return 1.0 / denom
   340	
   341	
   342	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   343	# Local effective Debye length
   344	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   345	
   346	def effective_debye_length_local(
   347	    *,
   348	    phi_o: float,
   349	    ctx: dict,
   350	    c_dyn_outer: list[float],
   351	    poisson_coeff: float,
   352	    dphi: float = 1e-4,
   353	) -> float:
   354	    """Local ``λ_eff = sqrt(eps / |dρ/dφ|_outer)`` via central FD.
   355	
   356	    Differs from the bulk ``Σ z² c`` Debye length by up to ~20× in 2:1
   357	    sulfate when ``|φ_o| ≳ 2`` because the steric closure depresses the
   358	    counterion contribution at strong ψ.  At I = 0.3 M with Stern
   359	    dominating, the correct screening coefficient is critical for the
   360	    linear-Debye Stern split.
   361	
   362	    Parameters
   363	    ----------
   364	    phi_o:
   365	        Outer-region equilibrium potential at which to evaluate
   366	        ``dρ/dφ`` (typically the value returned by
   367	        ``solve_outer_phi_multiion``).
   368	    ctx:
   369	        Counterion context from ``build_counterion_ctx``.
   370	    c_dyn_outer:
   371	        Dynamic-species concentrations at the OHP-edge outer region.
   372	    poisson_coeff:
   373	        Nondim Poisson coefficient (``ε * V_T / (F · c_scale · L²)``).
   374	    dphi:
   375	        Central FD step for evaluating ``dρ/dφ``.
   376	
   377	    Returns
   378	    -------
   379	    lambda_eff : float
   380	        Local effective Debye length (nondim).  Floored at 1e-15 to
   381	        avoid divide-by-zero when the local screening is degenerate.
   382	    """
   383	    rho_p = _electroneutrality_residual(phi=phi_o + dphi, ctx=ctx, c_dyn=c_dyn_outer)
   384	    rho_m = _electroneutrality_residual(phi=phi_o - dphi, ctx=ctx, c_dyn=c_dyn_outer)
   385	    drho_dphi = (rho_p - rho_m) / (2.0 * dphi)
   386	    # ε ∇²φ = -ρ ⇒ for small perturbation φ' ≈ ψ exp(-y/λ) with
   387	    # ε·(1/λ²) = -dρ/dφ ⇒ λ = sqrt(-ε / dρ/dφ).  dρ/dφ is negative
   388	    # in the screening regime (positive perturbation φ' attracts
   389	    # negative charge).  Take |dρ/dφ| to be safe.
   390	    inv_lambda_sq = max(-drho_dphi, 1e-30) / max(poisson_coeff, 1e-300)
   391	    return math.sqrt(1.0 / max(inv_lambda_sq, 1e-30))
   392	
   393	
   394	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   395	# Convenience: per-ion outer-region concentrations
   396	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   397	
   398	def per_ion_outer_concs(
   399	    *, ctx: dict, c_dyn_outer: list[float], phi_o: float,
   400	) -> list[float]:
   401	    """Evaluate every counterion's OHP-edge concentration at ``phi_o``.
   402	
   403	    The result mirrors the order of ``ctx['ions']`` and is the value
   404	    each ion contributes to the outer-region charge balance and the
   405	    multispecies γ_s denominator.
   406	    """
   407	    A_dyn_local = sum(a * c for a, c in zip(ctx["a_dyn"], c_dyn_outer))
   408	    denom = ctx["theta_b"] + sum(
   409	        ion["a_nondim"] * ion["c_bulk_nondim"] * _safe_exp(-ion["z"] * phi_o)
   410	        for ion in ctx["ions"] if ion.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"
   411	    )
   412	    return [
   413	        _ck_at_phi(
   414	            ion=ion, phi=phi_o, A_dyn_local=A_dyn_local,
   415	            theta_b=ctx["theta_b"], ions=ctx["ions"], denom_cache=denom,
   416	        )
   417	        for ion in ctx["ions"]
   418	    ]

    98	    z_dyn: list[int],
    99	    phi: Any,
   100	    R_space: Any,
   101	) -> list[StericBoltzmannBundle]:
   102	    """Build UFL closure expressions for steric-aware Boltzmann counterions.
   103	
   104	    Returns an empty list when no entries have ``steric_mode='bikerman'``.
   105	    The legacy single-counterion case (len == 1) reduces to the same
   106	    UFL algebra it always built; the bundle list contains exactly one
   107	    element. The multi-counterion shared-theta closure (plan §2.1)
   108	    extends this:
   109	
   110	    .. code-block:: text
   111	
   112	        For each analytic ion k (steric):
   113	          c_k(φ) = c_b_k · exp(-z_k·φ) · (1 - A_dyn(φ))
   114	                       / (θ_b + Σ_k' a_k' · c_b_k' · exp(-z_k'·φ))
   115	
   116	        with A_dyn(φ) = Σ_dyn a_i · c_i_dyn(φ)
   117	             θ_b      = 1 - A_dyn_bulk - Σ_k a_k · c_b_k
   118	
   119	    The denominator is the same for every steric ion (shared theta);
   120	    no coupled local NL solve needed.
   121	
   122	    Validates:
   123	        - ``θ_b > 0`` for the bulk (sum over ALL bikerman entries);
   124	          raises ``ValueError`` with a descriptive message otherwise.
   125	        - No double-counting: no bikerman entry's (z, c_bulk) may
   126	          duplicate any dynamic species' (z, c_bulk) within ``1e-9``
   127	          relative tolerance.
   128	
   129	    The (re)used ``ctx['boltzmann_z_scale']`` Function is the same
   130	    R-space scaling used by the legacy ideal path; both ideal and
   131	    bikerman counterions share it on the same ctx, so a single
   132	    ``_set_z_factor`` call ramps every contribution.
   133	
   134	    Returns
   135	    -------
   136	    list[StericBoltzmannBundle]
   137	        Empty list when no bikerman entries.  Otherwise one bundle per
   138	        bikerman counterion.  All bundles share the same z_scale.
   139	    """
   140	    counterions = _get_bv_boltzmann_counterions_cfg(params)
   141	    bikerman = [(j, e) for j, e in enumerate(counterions)
   142	                if e.get("steric_mode", "ideal") == "bikerman"]
   143	    if not bikerman:
   144	        return []
   145	
   146	    if not (len(a_dyn_floats) == len(c0_dyn) == len(z_dyn) == len(ci) == len(a_dyn_funcs)):
   147	        raise ValueError(
   148	            "build_steric_boltzmann_expressions: dynamic-species inputs misaligned "
   149	            f"(a_dyn_floats={len(a_dyn_floats)}, c0_dyn={len(c0_dyn)}, "
   150	            f"z_dyn={len(z_dyn)}, ci={len(ci)}, a_dyn_funcs={len(a_dyn_funcs)})"
   151	        )
   152	
   153	    # ----- bulk-side validation across ALL bikerman entries -----
   154	    A_dyn_bulk = sum(a * c for a, c in zip(a_dyn_floats, c0_dyn))
   155	    A_an_bulk = sum(
   156	        float(e["a_nondim"]) * float(e["c_bulk_nondim"]) for _, e in bikerman
   157	    )
   158	    theta_b = 1.0 - A_dyn_bulk - A_an_bulk
   159	    if theta_b <= 0.0:
   160	        bm_str = ", ".join(
   161	            f"a={float(e['a_nondim']):.4g}*c_b={float(e['c_bulk_nondim']):.4g}"
   162	            for _, e in bikerman
   163	        )
   164	        raise ValueError(
   165	            f"bikerman multi-counterion closure requires theta_b > 0, but got "
   166	            f"theta_b = 1 - A_dyn_bulk - sum(a_k*c_b_k) "
   167	            f"= 1 - {A_dyn_bulk:.6g} - {A_an_bulk:.6g} = {theta_b:.6g}; "
   168	            f"bikerman entries: [{bm_str}]; reduce dynamic-species packing, "
   169	            f"per-ion a_nondim, or per-ion c_bulk_nondim."
   170	        )
   171	
   172	    # Double-counting guard against EVERY dynamic species AND
   173	    # within-bikerman duplication (e.g. user lists Cs+ twice).
   174	    rel_tol = 1e-9
   175	    for k_idx, (j, entry) in enumerate(bikerman):
   176	        z_k = int(entry["z"])
   177	        c_k = float(entry["c_bulk_nondim"])
   178	        for i in range(len(c0_dyn)):
   179	            same_z = z_dyn[i] == z_k
   180	            denom = max(abs(c0_dyn[i]), abs(c_k), 1e-300)
   181	            same_c = abs(c0_dyn[i] - c_k) <= rel_tol * denom
   182	            if same_z and same_c:
   183	                raise ValueError(
   184	                    f"boltzmann_counterions[{j}] (z={z_k}, c_bulk={c_k}) "
   185	                    f"duplicates dynamic species[{i}] (z={z_dyn[i]}, "
   186	                    f"c_bulk={c0_dyn[i]}); remove from one or the other to "
   187	                    f"avoid double-counting in Poisson and steric packing."
   188	                )
   189	        for k2_idx, (j2, entry2) in enumerate(bikerman):
   190	            if k2_idx <= k_idx:
   191	                continue
   192	            z_k2 = int(entry2["z"])
   193	            c_k2 = float(entry2["c_bulk_nondim"])
   194	            denom = max(abs(c_k), abs(c_k2), 1e-300)
   195	            if z_k == z_k2 and abs(c_k - c_k2) <= rel_tol * denom:
   196	                raise ValueError(
   197	                    f"boltzmann_counterions[{j}] and [{j2}] duplicate "
   198	                    f"(z={z_k}, c_bulk={c_k}); remove one to avoid "
   199	                    f"double-counting."
   200	                )
   201	
   202	    # ----- shared UFL pieces (denominator + dynamic packing factor) -----
   203	    A_dyn_local = sum(a_dyn_funcs[i] * ci[i] for i in range(len(ci)))
   204	    free_dyn_floor = fd.Constant(1e-10)   # FE-interpolation safety on coarse meshes
   205	    free_dyn = fd.max_value(fd.Constant(1.0) - A_dyn_local, free_dyn_floor)
   206	    theta_b_const = fd.Constant(theta_b)
   207	
   208	    # Per-bikerman exponent uses each ion's OWN phi_clamp (each entry
   209	    # may set its own conservative clamp).  The SHARED denominator sums
   210	    # a_k * c_b_k * exp(-z_k * phi_clamped_k) — using each ion's clamp
   211	    # for its own term inside the sum is consistent with the closure
   212	    # derivation (the clamp only ever appears multiplied by that ion's
   213	    # z_k anyway, so the per-ion clamp is the right cap).
   214	    per_ion_q = []
   215	    for k_idx, (j, entry) in enumerate(bikerman):
   216	        z_k = int(entry["z"])
   217	        c_k = float(entry["c_bulk_nondim"])
   218	        a_k = float(entry["a_nondim"])
   219	        phi_clamp_k = float(entry["phi_clamp"])
   220	        z_k_const = fd.Constant(float(z_k))
   221	        c_k_const = fd.Constant(c_k)
   222	        a_k_const = fd.Constant(a_k)
   223	        phi_clamped_k = fd.min_value(
   224	            fd.max_value(phi, fd.Constant(-phi_clamp_k)),
   225	            fd.Constant(phi_clamp_k),
   226	        )
   227	        q_k = fd.exp(-z_k_const * phi_clamped_k)
   228	        per_ion_q.append({
   229	            "z_const": z_k_const,
   230	            "c_const": c_k_const,
   231	            "a_const": a_k_const,
   232	            "q": q_k,
   233	            "z": z_k,
   234	            "c_bulk": c_k,
   235	            "a_nondim": a_k,
   236	            "phi_clamp": phi_clamp_k,
   237	            "config_index": j,
   238	        })
   239	
   240	    denom = theta_b_const + sum(p["a_const"] * p["c_const"] * p["q"]
   241	                                for p in per_ion_q)
   242	
   243	    # Shared z_scale Function — single producer / single consumer.
   244	    if "boltzmann_z_scale" in ctx:
   245	        z_scale = ctx["boltzmann_z_scale"]
   246	    else:
   247	        z_scale = fd.Function(R_space, name="boltzmann_z_scale")
   248	        z_scale.assign(1.0)
   249	        ctx["boltzmann_z_scale"] = z_scale
   250	
   251	    bundles: list[StericBoltzmannBundle] = []
   252	    for p in per_ion_q:
   253	        c_steric_k = p["c_const"] * p["q"] * free_dyn / denom
   254	        bundles.append(StericBoltzmannBundle(
   255	            c_steric_expr=c_steric_k,
   256	            packing_contribution=p["a_const"] * c_steric_k,
   257	            charge_density=p["z_const"] * c_steric_k,
   258	            z_scale=z_scale,
   259	            metadata={
   260	                "config_index": p["config_index"],
   261	                "z": p["z"],
   262	                "c_bulk_nondim": p["c_bulk"],
   263	                "a_nondim": p["a_nondim"],
   264	                "phi_clamp": p["phi_clamp"],
   265	                "theta_b": theta_b,
   266	            },
   267	        ))
   268	    return bundles
   269	
   270	
   271	def add_boltzmann_counterion_residual(
   272	    ctx: dict[str, Any],
   273	    params: Any,
   274	    *,
   275	    skip_bikerman: bool = False,
   276	) -> int:
   277	    """Append analytic-Boltzmann counterion residuals to ``ctx['F_res']``.
   278	
   279	    Looks up ``params['bv_bc']['boltzmann_counterions']`` (parsed via
   280	    :func:`_get_bv_boltzmann_counterions_cfg`).  When non-empty, mutates

   920	    # rewritten as 2*ln((1+T*E)/(1-T*E)) to avoid atanh saturation at psi_D > ~30.
   921	    EPS_TANH = 1e-15

   923	    T_clamp = math.copysign(min(abs(T), 1.0 - EPS_TANH), T)

   975	        c_dyn_outer_at_ohp = [float(O_s), float(P_s), float(H_o)]
   976	        # Override Picard's 1:1-derived phi_o with the multi-ion solve.

   983	        lambda_eff = effective_debye_length_local(

   995	                / (poisson_coefficient + stern_coeff_val * lambda_eff)
   996	            )
   997	        else:
   998	            psi_D_local = full_drop
   999

  1003	        psi = fd.Constant(psi_D_local) * fd.exp(-y / fd.Constant(lambda_eff))
  1004	        # Outer-region φ profile: linear from phi_o_local at OHP to 0

   129	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   130	
   131	L_REF = 1.0e-4              # m (100 µm)
   132	D_REF = D_O2                # m²/s (O₂ diffusivity as reference)
   133	C_SCALE = C_O2              # mol/m³ (O₂ bulk concentration as reference)
   134	K_SCALE = D_REF / L_REF     # m/s (velocity scale for k0 nondimensionalization)
   135	
   136	
   137	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   138	# Dimensionless species properties
   139	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   140	
   141	D_O2_HAT = D_O2 / D_REF
   142	D_H2O2_HAT = D_H2O2 / D_REF
   143	D_HP_HAT = D_HP / D_REF
   144	D_CLO4_HAT = D_CLO4 / D_REF
   145	
   146	C_O2_HAT = C_O2 / C_SCALE
   147	C_H2O2_HAT = C_H2O2 / C_SCALE
   148	C_HP_HAT = C_HP / C_SCALE
   149	C_CLO4_HAT = C_CLO4 / C_SCALE
   150	
   151	K0_HAT_R1 = K0_PHYS_R1 / K_SCALE
   152	K0_HAT_R2 = K0_PHYS_R2 / K_SCALE
   153	# Parallel 2e/4e ORR nondimensional rate constants.
   154	K0_HAT_R2E = K0_PHYS_R2E / K_SCALE
   155	K0_HAT_R4E = K0_PHYS_R4E / K_SCALE
   156	
   157	# Steric (Bikerman) parameters
   158	A_DEFAULT = 0.01
   159	
   160	
   161	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   162	# Current density scale
   163	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   164	
   165	def compute_i_scale(
   166	    n_electrons: int = N_ELECTRONS,
   167	    d_ref: float = D_REF,
   168	    c_scale: float = C_SCALE,
   169	    l_ref: float = L_REF,
   170	) -> float:
   171	    """Compute current density conversion: dimensionless rate → mA/cm².
   172	
   173	    ``I_SCALE = n_e × F × D_ref × c_scale / L_ref × 0.1``
   174	    """
   175	    return n_electrons * F_CONST * d_ref * c_scale / l_ref * 0.1
   176	
   177	
   178	I_SCALE = compute_i_scale()
   179	
   180

   548	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   549	# Parallel 2e/4e ORR reaction set (Ruggiero 2022, M3a.2 — 2026-05-07)
   550	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   551	#
   552	# Used by passing ``bv_reactions=PARALLEL_2E_4E_REACTIONS`` to
   553	# ``make_bv_solver_params`` to override the legacy sequential R_1 + R_2
   554	# topology with the deck/paper-aligned parallel 2e + 4e topology.
   555	#
   556	# Stoichiometry conventions (per-species int list, length n_species=3):
   557	#   index 0 = O₂, index 1 = H₂O₂, index 2 = H⁺
   558	#   negative = consumed at cathode, positive = produced at cathode
   559	#
   560	# R_2e: O₂ + 2H⁺ + 2e⁻ → H₂O₂        stoichiometry [-1, +1, -2], n_e = 2
   561	# R_4e: O₂ + 4H⁺ + 4e⁻ → 2H₂O        stoichiometry [-1,  0, -4], n_e = 4
   562	#
   563	# H+ stoichiometric concentration factor is included on each reaction
   564	# with ``power = n_electrons`` (acid-form ORR consumes one H+ per electron).
   565	# Ruggiero §1 also lists alkaline-form rate laws; not modeled here.
   566	#
   567	# k0_R4e is a PRIOR-SELECTED placeholder (= K0_HAT_R2E) — not calibrated
   568	# to any data.  Per H18 V4: k0_4e is weakly identified from page-15
   569	# peroxide alone; calibrate against disk current / selectivity / Tafel
   570	# slope in M4.  Sweep K0_HAT_R4E ∈ {1, 5, 10} × K0_HAT_R2E in M3a.2 if
   571	# magnitude is far off experimental.
   572	
   573	PARALLEL_2E_4E_REACTIONS: List[Dict[str, Any]] = [
   574	    {
   575	        "k0": K0_HAT_R2E,
   576	        "alpha": ALPHA_R2E,
   577	        "cathodic_species": 0,           # O₂
   578	        "anodic_species": 1,             # H₂O₂ (reverse direction)
   579	        "c_ref": 1.0,
   580	        "stoichiometry": [-1, +1, -2],   # O₂ consumed, H₂O₂ produced, 2 H⁺ consumed
   581	        "n_electrons": 2,
   582	        "reversible": True,
   583	        "E_eq_v": E_EQ_R2E_V,            # 0.695 V vs RHE
   584	        "cathodic_conc_factors": [
   585	            {"species": 2, "power": 2, "c_ref_nondim": C_HP_HAT},
   586	        ],
   587	    },
   588	    {
   589	        "k0": K0_HAT_R4E,
   590	        "alpha": ALPHA_R4E,
   591	        "cathodic_species": 0,           # O₂
   592	        "anodic_species": None,          # irreversible to water
   593	        "c_ref": 0.0,
   594	        "stoichiometry": [-1,  0, -4],   # O₂ consumed, H₂O₂ untouched, 4 H⁺ consumed
   595	        "n_electrons": 4,
   596	        "reversible": False,
   597	        "E_eq_v": E_EQ_R4E_V,            # 1.23 V vs RHE
   598	        "cathodic_conc_factors": [
   599	            {"species": 2, "power": 4, "c_ref_nondim": C_HP_HAT},
   600	        ],
   601	    },
   602	]

   102	def _make_sp(*, k0_r2e_factor: float, k0_r4e_factor: float):
   103	    from scripts._bv_common import (
   104	        SNES_OPTS_CHARGED,
   105	        THREE_SPECIES_LOGC_BOLTZMANN,
   106	        DEFAULT_CSPLUS_BOLTZMANN_COUNTERION_STERIC,
   107	        DEFAULT_SULFATE_BOLTZMANN_COUNTERION_STERIC,
   108	        make_bv_solver_params,
   109	    )
   110	    snes_opts = {**SNES_OPTS_CHARGED}
   111	    snes_opts.update({
   112	        "snes_max_it":               400,
   113	        "snes_atol":                 1e-7,
   114	        "snes_rtol":                 1e-10,
   115	        "snes_stol":                 1e-12,
   116	        "snes_linesearch_type":      "l2",
   117	        "snes_linesearch_maxlambda": 0.3,
   118	        "snes_divergence_tolerance": 1e10,
   119	    })
   120	    rxns = _build_parallel_reactions(
   121	        k0_factor_R2e=k0_r2e_factor, k0_factor_R4e=k0_r4e_factor,
   122	    )
   123	    sp = make_bv_solver_params(
   124	        eta_hat=0.0, dt=0.25, t_end=80.0,
   125	        species=THREE_SPECIES_LOGC_BOLTZMANN,
   126	        snes_opts=snes_opts,
   127	        formulation=FORMULATION, log_rate=True,
   128	        u_clamp=U_CLAMP,
   129	        bv_reactions=rxns,
   130	        boltzmann_counterions=[
   131	            DEFAULT_CSPLUS_BOLTZMANN_COUNTERION_STERIC,
   132	            DEFAULT_SULFATE_BOLTZMANN_COUNTERION_STERIC,
   133	        ],
   134	        multi_ion_enabled=True,             # plan §2.2/§2.3 opt-in
   135	        stern_capacitance_f_m2=0.10,
   136	        initializer=INITIALIZER,
   137	    )
   138	    new_opts = dict(sp.solver_options)
   139	    new_bv = dict(new_opts["bv_convergence"])
   140	    new_bv["exponent_clip"] = float(EXPONENT_CLIP)
   141	    new_opts["bv_convergence"] = new_bv
   142	    return sp.with_solver_options(new_opts)

   234	    def _build_eta_clipped(E_eq_const):
   235	        """Build clipped overpotential expression for a given E_eq.
   236	
   237	        Note: clip is applied to ``eta_scaled = (V - E_eq) / V_T``, NOT to the
   238	        full BV exponent ``alpha * n_e * eta_scaled``. So a reaction's BV
   239	        exponent unclips when ``|V - E_eq| < exponent_clip * V_T``.
   240	        For exponent_clip=50, V_T=0.02569 V, E_eq_2=1.78 V, this gives
   241	        V_unclip_2 = 1.78 - 50*0.02569 = +0.495 V (R2 unclipping threshold).
   242	        """
   243	        if use_stern:
   244	            eta_raw = phi_applied_func - phi - E_eq_const
   245	        elif conv_cfg["use_eta_in_bv"]:

   252	            return fd.min_value(fd.max_value(eta_scaled, -clip_val), clip_val)

   268	    # count.  Returns None when no bikerman entries are configured —

   287	        if steric_boltz:

   289	            # by the same ``boltzmann_z_scale`` Function the Poisson

   307	    # Residual: Nernst-Planck with log-concentration transform

   441	                else:

   452	                elif rxn["reversible"] and float(rxn["c_ref_model"]) > 1e-30:
   453	                    c_ref_j_log = fd.ln(fd.Constant(float(rxn["c_ref_model"])))
   454	                    log_anodic = (
   455	                        fd.ln(k0_j) + c_ref_j_log
   456	                        + (fd.Constant(1.0) - alpha_j) * n_e_j * eta_j
   457	                    )
   458	                    anodic = fd.exp(log_anodic)
   459	                else:
   460	                    anodic = fd.Constant(0.0)
   461	            else:
   462	                # Cathodic term: k0 * c_cat * exp(-alpha * n_e * eta)
   463	                # c_surf[mu_h_idx] is muh-reconstructed; transparent here.
   464	                cathodic = k0_j * c_surf[cat_idx] * fd.exp(-alpha_j * n_e_j * eta_j)
   465	
   466	                # Cathodic concentration factors
   467	                for factor in rxn.get("cathodic_conc_factors", []):
   468	                    sp_idx = factor["species"]
   469	                    power = factor["power"]
   470	                    c_ref_f = fd.Constant(max(float(factor["c_ref_nondim"]), 1e-12))
   471	                    cathodic = cathodic * (c_surf[sp_idx] / c_ref_f) ** power
   472	
   473	                # Anodic term (if reversible)
   474	                if rxn["reversible"] and rxn["anodic_species"] is not None:
   475	                    anod_idx = rxn["anodic_species"]
   476	                    anodic = k0_j * c_surf[anod_idx] * fd.exp(
   477	                        (fd.Constant(1.0) - alpha_j) * n_e_j * eta_j
   478	                    )
   479	                elif rxn["reversible"]:
   480	                    c_ref_j = fd.Constant(float(rxn["c_ref_model"]))
   481	                    anodic = k0_j * c_ref_j * fd.exp(
   482	                        (fd.Constant(1.0) - alpha_j) * n_e_j * eta_j
   483	                    )
   484	                else:
   485	                    anodic = fd.Constant(0.0)
   486	
   487	            R_j = cathodic - anodic
   488	            bv_rate_exprs.append(R_j)
   489	
   490	            stoi = rxn["stoichiometry"]
   491	            for i in range(n):
   492	                if stoi[i] != 0:
   493	                    F_res -= fd.Constant(float(stoi[i])) * R_j * v_list[i] * ds(electrode_marker)
   494	
   495	    else:

    46	
    47	def _eta_clipped(
    48	    *,
    49	    eta_drop: float,
    50	    E: float,
    51	    bv_exp_scale: float,
    52	    exponent_clip: float,
    53	    clip: bool,
    54	) -> float:
    55	    """Compute clipped overpotential ``bv_exp_scale * (eta_drop - E)``.
    56	
    57	    ``eta_drop`` is the potential drop the Butler-Volmer reaction "sees":
    58	
    59	      - No-Stern (legacy): ``eta_drop = phi_applied`` (residual sets
    60	        ``eta_raw = phi_applied - E``).
    61	      - Stern: ``eta_drop = psi_S = phi_applied - phi_surface`` (residual
    62	        sets ``eta_raw = phi_applied - phi - E`` with ``phi`` at the OHP).
    63	
    64	    The clip is applied to the scaled raw eta, NOT to ``alpha * n_e * eta``;
    65	    see ``docs/clipping_conventions.md``.
    66	    """
    67	    eta = bv_exp_scale * (eta_drop - E)
    68	    if clip:
    69	        return max(min(eta, exponent_clip), -exponent_clip)
    70	    return eta

    81	
    82	      (a) supports any reactant species in cathodic_conc_factors (e.g. an
    83	          O2 stoichiometric factor in a future config); and
    84	      (b) eliminates ``H_s = H_o * exp(-psi_D)`` as a hidden gamma-free
    85	          shortcut. Callers are responsible for building ``log_by_species``
    86	          with or without ``log(gamma_s)`` folded in.
    87	    """
    88	    total = 0.0
    89	    for f in factors:
    90	        sp_idx = int(f["species"])
